   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    List of spacewalks and moonwalks 1965–1999
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div class="noprint" id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       For later spacewalks, see
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_spacewalks_2000%E2%80%932014" title="List of spacewalks 2000–2014">
        List of spacewalks 2000–2014
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_spacewalks_since_2015" title="List of spacewalks since 2015">
        List of spacewalks since 2015
       </a>
       .
      </div>
      <p>
       This list contains all
       <b>
        spacewalks and moonwalks
       </b>
       performed from 1965 to 1999 where an
       <a href="/wiki/Astronaut" title="Astronaut">
        astronaut
       </a>
       has fully or partially left a spacecraft. Entries for moonwalks are shown with a gray background while entries for all other
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra-vehicular_activity" title="Extra-vehicular activity">
        EVAs
       </a>
       are uncolored.
      </p>
      <p>
       All
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spacewalk" title="Spacewalk">
        spacewalks
       </a>
       have had the astronauts tethered to their
       <a href="/wiki/Spacecraft" title="Spacecraft">
        spacecraft
       </a>
       except for seven spacewalks by the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
        United States
       </a>
       (six in 1984 using the
       <a href="/wiki/Manned_Maneuvering_Unit" title="Manned Maneuvering Unit">
        Manned Maneuvering Unit
       </a>
       , and one in 1994 testing the
       <a href="/wiki/Simplified_Aid_For_EVA_Rescue" title="Simplified Aid For EVA Rescue">
        SAFER
       </a>
       rescue device). All moonwalks were performed with astronauts untethered, and some of the astronauts traveled far enough to lose visual contact with their craft (they were up to 7.6 km away from it using the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lunar_Rover" title="Lunar Rover">
        Lunar Rover
       </a>
       ). One lunar EVA was not a moonwalk, but rather a stand-up EVA partially out the top hatch of the LM, where it was thought that the extra height would help with surveying the area prior to conducting the moonwalks. Only three deep-space EVAs have ever been conducted, where the activity was neither on the lunar surface nor in Low Earth Orbit, but far away from both the Moon and the Earth.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <h2>
       <span id="1965.E2.80.931969_spacewalks_and_moonwalks">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="1965–1969_spacewalks_and_moonwalks">
        1965–1969 spacewalks and moonwalks
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spacewalks_and_moonwalks_1965%E2%80%931999&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: 1965–1969 spacewalks and moonwalks">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       <i>
        Spacewalk beginning and ending times are given in
        <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">
         Coordinated Universal Time
        </a>
        (UTC).
       </i>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <tr style="background:#ccf;">
        <td>
         <center>
          <b>
           #
          </b>
         </center>
        </td>
        <td>
         <center>
          <b>
           Spacecraft
          </b>
         </center>
        </td>
        <td>
         <center>
          <b>
           Spacewalkers
          </b>
         </center>
        </td>
        <td>
         <center>
          <b>
           Start (
           <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">
            UTC
           </a>
           )
          </b>
         </center>
        </td>
        <td>
         <center>
          <b>
           End (UTC)
          </b>
         </center>
        </td>
        <td>
         <center>
          <b>
           Duration
          </b>
         </center>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td rowspan="2">
         1.
        </td>
        <td rowspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Voskhod_2" title="Voskhod 2">
          Voskhod 2
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
           <img alt="Soviet Union" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union_%281955-1980%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union_%281955-1980%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union_%281955-1980%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union_%281955-1980%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union_%281955-1980%29.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_Soviet_Union_%281955-1980%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Alexey_Leonov" title="Alexey Leonov">
          Alexey Leonov
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         18 March 1965
         <br/>
         08:34:51
        </td>
        <td>
         18 March 1965
         <br/>
         08:47:00
        </td>
        <td>
         0 h 12 min
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Leonov conducted the first
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra-vehicular_activity" title="Extra-vehicular activity">
          EVA
         </a>
         in history.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-voskhod2_1-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-voskhod2-1">
           [1]
          </a>
         </sup>
         Leonov had difficulty fitting back into the spacecraft due to spacesuit stiffness in vacuum, and vented air from his spacesuit in order to bend back into the capsule.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
          <a href="#cite_note-2">
           [2]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td rowspan="2">
         2.
        </td>
        <td rowspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Gemini_4" title="Gemini 4">
          Gemini 4
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Ed_White_(astronaut)" title="Ed White (astronaut)">
          Ed White
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         3 June 1965
         <br/>
         19:46:00
        </td>
        <td>
         3 June 1965
         <br/>
         20:06:00
        </td>
        <td>
         0 h 20 min
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         White conducted the second EVA in history and the first American EVA.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
          <a href="#cite_note-3">
           [3]
          </a>
         </sup>
         White also had difficulty returning to the Gemini spacecraft. Although he was very fit and athletic, the effort left him exhausted.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
          <a href="#cite_note-4">
           [4]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="6" style="background:#ccf; height:5px;">
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td rowspan="2">
         3.
        </td>
        <td rowspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Gemini_9A" title="Gemini 9A">
          Gemini 9A
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Eugene_Cernan" title="Eugene Cernan">
          Eugene Cernan
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         5 June 1966
         <br/>
         15:02:00
        </td>
        <td>
         5 June 1966
         <br/>
         17:09:00
        </td>
        <td>
         2 h 7 min
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         A complex work EVA was planned for Cernan, which involved him moving to the rear of the Gemini spacecraft and donning the
         <a href="/wiki/Astronaut_propulsion_unit" title="Astronaut propulsion unit">
          Astronaut propulsion unit
         </a>
         , developed by the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Air_Force" title="U.S. Air Force">
          U.S. Air Force
         </a>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
          <a href="#cite_note-5">
           [5]
          </a>
         </sup>
         Cernan expended four to five times the expected effort, raising his pulse as high as 180 beats per minute. Excess heat and respiration completely fogged Cernan's visor, and the EVA was cut short. Cernan also had difficulty returning to the spacecraft and closing the hatch.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
          <a href="#cite_note-6">
           [6]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td rowspan="2">
         4.
        </td>
        <td rowspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Gemini_10" title="Gemini 10">
          Gemini 10
         </a>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Collins performed a stand-up EVA. Instead of climbing completely out of the spacecraft, Collins extended his torso outside the spacecraft to take photos before and after capsule sunrise. Color photography after sunrise was only partly completed due to severe eye irritation of both Collins and Command Pilot
         <a href="/wiki/John_Young_(astronaut)" title="John Young (astronaut)">
          Young
         </a>
         . Handling the camera proved difficult due to the stiffness of Collins' gloves.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
          <a href="#cite_note-7">
           [7]
          </a>
         </sup>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Collins performed an umbilical EVA. With more difficulty than expected, Collins collected the micrometeorite collection package from the exterior of the Gemini spacecraft. Then, using the Hand Held Maneuvering Unit, he pushed to the nearby
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agena_Target_Vehicle" title="Agena Target Vehicle">
          Agena Target Vehicle
         </a>
         to collect its micrometeorite collection package. Collins then pulled on the umbilical cord to return and re-enter the spacecraft.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
          <a href="#cite_note-8">
           [8]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Gordon attached a tether between the Gemini and Agena Target Vehicle for later orbital mechanics testing. While making the attachment, his workload exceeded the capacity of the spacesuit cooling system, and his vision became obscured by a fogged visor and sweat in his eyes. Planned activities were curtailed by Command Pilot
         <a href="/wiki/Pete_Conrad" title="Pete Conrad">
          Conrad
         </a>
         and Gordon returned to the spacecraft.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
          <a href="#cite_note-9">
           [9]
          </a>
         </sup>

        <td colspan="4">
         Aldrin performed a stand-up EVA. Aldrin took UV still photos and 16 mm color movie pictures, collected external experimental samples, and conducted a light exercise routine.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
          <a href="#cite_note-11">
           [11]
          </a>

          Gemini 12
         </a>
         – EVA 2
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>

         13 November 1966
         <br/>
         15:34:00

        <td>
         13 November 1966
         <br/>
         17:40:00
        </td>
        <td>
         2 h 06 min
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Aldrin’s walk was the first completely successful umbilical EVA, with all objectives achieved. He was able to control his movements and restrict his workload using techniques developed using underwater zero gravity simulations. Aldrin also benefited from the experiences of the previous American EVAs. Aldrin was able to move around the outside of the craft, deploy and recover various experimental packages, install and remove cameras, and practice work techniques using a ratchet-type wrench.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
          <a href="#cite_note-12">
           [12]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Aldrin performed another stand-up EVA. Aldrin again extended outside the hatch to take photographs and repeat the light exercise experiment. Exertion levels during exercise were comparable to preflight simulations. Equipment and waste food containers not needed for re-entry were jettisoned from the spacecraft.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
          <a href="#cite_note-13">
           [13]
          </a>
         </sup>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Khrunov and Yeliseyev conducted the first two-man spacewalk. Both cosmonauts launched in Soyuz 5, which then docked with Soyuz 4. Khrunov and Yeliseyev performed an EVA to transfer to Soyuz 4. Although docked together, Soyuz 4 and Soyuz 5 did not make an internal connection, necessitating the EVA. Khrunov and Yeliseyev returned to Earth aboard Soyuz 4.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
          <a href="#cite_note-14">
           [14]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Schweickart exited the
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Lunar_Module" title="Apollo Lunar Module">
          Lunar Module
         </a>
         hatch, wearing the
         <a href="/wiki/Primary_Life_Support_System" title="Primary Life Support System">
          Portable Life Support System
         </a>
         (PLSS) backpack. Schweickart's backpack provided oxygen, communications, and cooling, independent of his spacecraft. Scott extended out of the
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Command/Service_Module" title="Apollo Command/Service Module">
          Command Module
         </a>
         hatch but remained supported by the Command Module through an umbilical cord. Plans for Schweickart to move to the Command Module hatch were scrubbed due to severe
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Space_sickness" title="Space sickness">
          space sickness
         </a>
         he had suffered the day before.

          <a href="#cite_note-15">
           [15]
          </a>
         </sup>

        <td>
         21 July 1969
         <br/>
         05:11:13
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">

          </a>
         </sup>

         2 h 31 min 40 s
        </td>

       <tr style="background:silver;">
        <td colspan="4">
         Armstrong became the first man to walk on the Moon. Aldrin followed, describing the Moon as "magnificent desolation."
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apollo11a_17-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-apollo11a-17">
           [17]
          </a>
         </sup>
         During their 2½ hour EVA, the team deployed the Early Apollo Scientific Experimental Package, took a call from
         <a href="/wiki/Richard_Nixon" title="Richard Nixon">
          President Nixon
         </a>
         , collected rock and core samples, raised a
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_Flag" title="US Flag">
          US Flag
         </a>
         , and took photographs.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
          <a href="#cite_note-18">
           [18]
          </a>
         </sup>
         Armstrong reported moving around on the Moon was easier than the simulation.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apollo11a_17-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-apollo11a-17">
           [17]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr style="background:silver;">
        <td rowspan="2">

        </td>

          </a>

         <a href="/wiki/Alan_Bean" title="Alan Bean">
          Alan Bean
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         19 November 1969
         <br/>
         11:32:35
        </td>
        <td>
         19 November 1969
         <br/>
         15:28:38
        </td>
        <td>
         3 h 56 min 03 s
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr style="background:silver;">
        <td colspan="4">
         During the first Apollo 12 moonwalk, Conrad and Bean deployed the Modular Equipment Stowage Assembly, collected and stowed the contingency sample, erected the solar wind foil, collected core samples and more surface samples, and deployed the
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Lunar_Surface_Experiments_Package" title="Apollo Lunar Surface Experiments Package">
          Apollo Lunar Surface Experiments Package
         </a>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
          <a href="#cite_note-19">
           [19]
          </a>
         </sup>
         Early in the moonwalk, Bean accidentally pointed the color TV camera toward the Sun and destroyed the camera. Communication to the ground for the remainder of their moonwalks became radio-only.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
          <a href="#cite_note-20">
           [20]
          </a>
         </sup>
         The two were surprised to find photocopies of Playboy Playmate pictures inserted into some pages of their cuff checklist, a prank done by their backup crew.
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr style="background:silver;">
        <td rowspan="2">
         15.
        </td>
        <td rowspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_12" title="Apollo 12">
          Apollo 12
         </a>
         – Second moonwalk
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Pete_Conrad" title="Pete Conrad">
          Pete Conrad
         </a>
         <br/>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Alan_Bean" title="Alan Bean">
          Alan Bean
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         November 20, 1969
         <br/>
         03:54:45
        </td>
        <td>
         November 20, 1969
         <br/>
         07:44:00
        </td>
        <td>
         3 h 49 min 15 s
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr style="background:silver;">
        <td colspan="4">
         Conrad and Bean collected additional core and rock samples and traveled over 600 feet (180 m) to
         <a href="/wiki/Surveyor_3" title="Surveyor 3">
          Surveyor 3
         </a>
         to collect some parts (including the TV camera) off the robotic lander. They also retrieved the solar wind foil deployed on their earlier moonwalk.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
          <a href="#cite_note-21">
           [21]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>

      <h2>
       <span id="1970.E2.80.931979_spacewalks_and_moonwalks">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="1970–1979_spacewalks_and_moonwalks">
        1970–1979 spacewalks and moonwalks
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spacewalks_and_moonwalks_1965%E2%80%931999&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1970–1979 spacewalks and moonwalks">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       <i>
        Spacewalk beginning and ending times are given in
        <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">
         Coordinated Universal Time
        </a>
        (UTC).
       </i>
      </p>

       <tr style="background:silver;">
        <td rowspan="2">
         16.
        </td>
        <td rowspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_14" title="Apollo 14">
          Apollo 14
         </a>
         <br/>
         First moonwalk
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shepard" title="Alan Shepard">
          Alan Shepard
         </a>
         <br/>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Mitchell" title="Edgar Mitchell">
          Edgar Mitchell
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         February 5, 1971
         <br/>
         14:42:13
        </td>
        <td>
         February 5, 1971
         <br/>
         19:30:50
        </td>
        <td>
         4 h 47 min 50 s
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr style="background:silver;">
        <td colspan="4">
         Shepard and Mitchell deployed the Modular Equipment Stowage Assembly, grabbed a contingency sample, and successfully set up the color TV camera. They erected an American flag and the solar wind foil. They then deployed the
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Lunar_Surface_Experiments_Package" title="Apollo Lunar Surface Experiments Package">
          ALSEP
         </a>
         and proceeded to collect core samples and several large moon rocks.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
          <a href="#cite_note-22">
           [22]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr style="background:silver;">
        <td rowspan="2">
         17.
        </td>
        <td rowspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_14" title="Apollo 14">
          Apollo 14
         </a>
         <br/>
         Second moonwalk
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Alan_Shepard" title="Alan Shepard">
          Alan Shepard
         </a>
         <br/>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Mitchell" title="Edgar Mitchell">
          Edgar Mitchell
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         February 6, 1971
         <br/>
         08:11:15
        </td>
        <td>
         February 6, 1971
         <br/>
         12:45:56
        </td>
        <td>
         4 h 34 min 41 s
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr style="background:silver;">
        <td colspan="4">
         Shepard and Mitchell trekked 1300 meters (almost a mile) up the side of Cone crater, collecting rock samples, taking photographs and deploying a portable magnetometer. Although they came close, the team didn’t find the rim of the crater due to the difficulty of navigating the stark lunarscape.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
          <a href="#cite_note-23">
           [23]
          </a>
         </sup>
         Before re-entering the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lunar_Module" title="Lunar Module">
          Lunar Module
         </a>
         , Shepard used a modified sample tool to hit a couple of golf balls.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
          <a href="#cite_note-24">
           [24]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td rowspan="2">
         18.
        </td>
        <td rowspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_15" title="Apollo 15">
          Apollo 15
         </a>
         <br/>
         Stand up EVA
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/David_Scott" title="David Scott">
          David Scott
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         July 31, 1971
         <br/>
         00:16:49
        </td>
        <td>
         July 31, 1971
         <br/>
         00:49:56
        </td>
        <td>
         33 min 07 s
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Scott stood in the top hatch of the Lunar Module, visually surveying and photographing the landing site. He identified future EVA destinations and confirmed suitability for
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lunar_Rover" title="Lunar Rover">
          Lunar Rover
         </a>
         access.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
          <a href="#cite_note-25">
           [25]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr style="background:silver;">
        <td rowspan="2">
         19.
        </td>
        <td rowspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_15" title="Apollo 15">
          Apollo 15
         </a>
         <br/>
         First moonwalk
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/David_Scott" title="David Scott">
          David Scott
         </a>
         <br/>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/James_Irwin" title="James Irwin">
          James Irwin
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         July 31, 1971
         <br/>
         13:12:17
        </td>
        <td>
         July 31, 1971
         <br/>
         19:45:59
        </td>
        <td>
         6 h 32 min 42 s
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr style="background:silver;">
        <td colspan="4">
         Scott and Irwin were the first team to ride the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lunar_Rover" title="Lunar Rover">
          Lunar Rover
         </a>
         on the moon. After securing the contingency sample, they drove the rover (equipped with a TV camera beaming video back to Houston) to Elbow Crater and then to St. George Crater, collecting rock samples and taking photographs on the 5.6-mile (9.0 km) trip. On return to the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lunar_Module" title="Lunar Module">
          Lunar Module
         </a>
         , the moonwalkers deployed the
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Lunar_Surface_Experiments_Package" title="Apollo Lunar Surface Experiments Package">
          ALSEP
         </a>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
          <a href="#cite_note-26">
           [26]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr style="background:silver;">
        <td rowspan="2">
         20.
        </td>
        <td rowspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_15" title="Apollo 15">
          Apollo 15
         </a>
         <br/>
         Second moonwalk
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/David_Scott" title="David Scott">
          David Scott
         </a>
         <br/>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/James_Irwin" title="James Irwin">
          James Irwin
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         August 1, 1971
         <br/>
         11:48:48
        </td>
        <td>
         August 1, 1971
         <br/>
         19:01:02
        </td>
        <td>
         7 h 12 min 14 s
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr style="background:silver;">
        <td colspan="4">
         Scott and Irwin traveled a southbound loop of 6.8 miles (10.9 km) in the Lunar Rover, collecting rock and soil samples, photographs, and a core sample. They stopped at the Apennine front, Spur Crater, and Dune Crater. At the Spur Crater rim Scott and Irwin spotted and collected a white rock later estimated to be 4.5 billion years old. Almost as old as the Moon itself, sample 15415 has become known as
         <i>
          Genesis Rock
         </i>
         , the oldest rock recovered during the Apollo missions.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
          <a href="#cite_note-27">
           [27]
          </a>
         </sup>
         After returning to the Lunar Module, they completed work around the
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Lunar_Surface_Experiments_Package" title="Apollo Lunar Surface Experiments Package">
          ALSEP
         </a>
         before re-entering the LM.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
          <a href="#cite_note-28">
           [28]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr style="background:silver;">
        <td rowspan="2">
         21.
        </td>
        <td rowspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Apollo_15" title="Apollo 15">
          Apollo 15
         </a>
         <br/>
         Third moonwalk
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/David_Scott" title="David Scott">
          David Scott
         </a>
         <br/>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/James_Irwin" title="James Irwin">
          James Irwin
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         August 2, 1971
         <br/>
         08:52:14
        </td>
        <td>
         August 2, 1971
         <br/>
         13:42:04
        </td>
        <td>
         4 h 49 min 50 s
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr style="background:silver;">
        <td colspan="4">
         The spacewalkers' last Lunar Rover ride traveled 2.8 miles (4.5 km) westward toward
         <a href="/wiki/Mons_Hadley" title="Mons Hadley">
          Hadley Rille
         </a>
         . Sample collections and photographs were taken at Scarp Crater, Rim Crater, and The Terrace on the rim of the Hadley Rille. Returning to the Lunar Module, Scott and Irwin collected the long core sample from the area of the ALSEP.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
          <a href="#cite_note-29">
           [29]
          </a>
         </sup>

         </a>

         Young and Duke climbed back onto the

         </a>
         and traveled to Palmetto and End Crater, finally reaching the rim of North Ray Crater.

          </a>

           [36]
          </a>
         </sup>

        <td colspan="4">
         On their last moonwalk, Cernan and Schmitt drove the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lunar_Rover" title="Lunar Rover">

         </a>
         toward the
         <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=North_Massif&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="North Massif (page does not exist)">

         </a>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
          <a href="#cite_note-40">
           [40]
          </a>
         </sup>
         They explored a large split boulder called Tracy’s Rock, (named for Cernan’s daughter) taking samples, making photographs, and providing oral descriptions of the area.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ALSJend_39-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-ALSJend-39">
           [39]
          </a>
         </sup>
         The moonwalkers also visited the Sculptured Hills and Van Serg Crater as they finished their 7.5 miles (12.1 km) final ride.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A17MR_38-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-A17MR-38">
           [38]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">
          :
          <span>
           pp. 10–16
          </span>
         </sup>
         Cernan is the last person to date to walk on the lunar surface.
        </td>
       </tr>

      <h2>
       <span id="1980.E2.80.931984_spacewalks">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="1980–1984_spacewalks">
        1980–1984 spacewalks
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spacewalks_and_moonwalks_1965%E2%80%931999&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1980–1984 spacewalks">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       <i>
        Spacewalk beginning and ending times are given in
        <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">
         Coordinated Universal Time
        </a>
        (UTC).
       </i>
      </p>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Performing the first
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra-vehicular_activity" title="Extra-vehicular activity">
          EVA
         </a>
         from
         <a href="/wiki/Salyut_7" title="Salyut 7">
          Salyut 7
         </a>
         , Lebedev anchored himself with a foot restraint, while Berezovoy assisted from the hatch. After collecting and placing samples on the exterior surface of the spacecraft, Lebedev tested methods for assembly and disassembly work in space, including the Istok panel experiment of turning bolts with a special wrench.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
          <a href="#cite_note-54">
           [54]
          </a>
         </sup>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Nelson rode the
         <a href="/wiki/Manned_Maneuvering_Unit" title="Manned Maneuvering Unit">
          MMU
         </a>
         to the
         <a href="/wiki/Solar_Maximum_Mission" title="Solar Maximum Mission">
          SMM
         </a>
         satellite. Van Hoften stood by in the payload bay to provide any needed assistance. After three unsuccessful attempts to capture the SMM with the Trunnion Pin Acquisition Device (TPAD) tool and one attempt to grab the satellite by hand, the spacewalkers returned to
         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger" title="Space Shuttle Challenger">
          <i>
           Challenger
          </i>
         </a>
         . The SMM was recovered the next day with the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Remote_Manipulator_System" title="Remote Manipulator System">
          RMS
         </a>
         .

          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Remote_Manipulator_System" title="Remote Manipulator System">
           Remote Manipulator System
          </a>
          foot restraint in the payload bay of
          <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Challenger" title="Space Shuttle Challenger">
           <i>
            Challenger
           </i>
          </a>
          during
          <a href="/wiki/STS-41-B" title="STS-41-B">
           STS-41-B
          </a>
          .
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span id="1985.E2.80.931989_spacewalks">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="1985–1989_spacewalks">
        1985–1989 spacewalks
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spacewalks_and_moonwalks_1965%E2%80%931999&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1985–1989 spacewalks">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       <i>
        Spacewalk beginning and ending times are given in
        <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">
         Coordinated Universal Time
        </a>
        (UTC).
       </i>
      </p>

          </a>
         </span>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Hoffman" title="Jeffrey Hoffman">
          Jeffrey Hoffman
         </a>
         <br/>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/S._David_Griggs" title="S. David Griggs">
          S. David Griggs
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         16 April 1985
        </td>
        <td>
         16 April 1985
        </td>
        <td>
         3 h 06 min
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Griggs and Hoffman installed an improvised switch-pulling tool, called the "flyswatter", on
         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Discovery" title="Space Shuttle Discovery">
          <i>
           Discovery
          </i>
         </a>
         's
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Remote_Manipulator_System" title="Remote Manipulator System">
          RMS
         </a>
         robotic arm. The "flyswatter" was used in an effort to push the sequencer start lever on the Syncom IV-3 satellite in the proper position for deployment.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
          <a href="#cite_note-65">
           [65]
          </a>
         </sup>
         This attempted repair was the first unplanned spacewalk in NASA history.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
          <a href="#cite_note-66">
           [66]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Van Hoften rode the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Remote_Manipulator_System" title="Remote Manipulator System">
          RMS
         </a>
         to capture the
         <a href="/wiki/Syncom" title="Syncom">
          Syncom
         </a>
         IV-3 satellite and pulled it into
         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Discovery" title="Space Shuttle Discovery">
          <i>
           Discovery
          </i>
         </a>
         's payload bay. Fisher and Van Hoften then secured and started repairs on the satellite in the payload bay. The retrieval was complicated by a malfunction of the RMS that made hindered its operation.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts-51i_68-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-sts-51i-68">
           [68]

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Fisher and Van Hoften completed repairs on the
         <a href="/wiki/Syncom" title="Syncom">
          Syncom
         </a>
         IV-3 satellite. Then Van Hoften, riding the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Remote_Manipulator_System" title="Remote Manipulator System">
          RMS
         </a>
         , heaved the satellite out of the payload bay, imparting the spin needed for the satellite to fire its perigee motor.

         </a>

        <td colspan="4">
         Titov and Manarov attempted to replace
         <a href="/wiki/Kvant-1" title="Kvant-1">
          Kvant
         </a>
         's X-ray telescope during a spacewalk that was not planned or rehearsed before launch. They trained by watching a videotape and talking to
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cosmonauts" title="Cosmonauts">
          cosmonauts
         </a>
         who had practiced the repair in a pool. The repair ended prematurely when a special wrench broke.

          <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
           <img alt="France" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>

         <br/>
         15:57

         6 h 00 min
        </td>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         The first EVA by a French citizen commenced when Volkov and Chrétien ventured outside
         <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">
          Mir
         </a>
         to install hardware and experiments. The Soviet-French spacewalking team installed handrails, installed and wired the Enchantillons rack, and installed the ERA experimental package. At first, the ERA package failed to unfold when commanded from inside Mir. A swift kick from Volkov was needed for it to properly unfold.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
          <a href="#cite_note-75">
           [75]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>

          <a href="/wiki/Jerry_L._Ross" title="Jerry L. Ross">
           Jerry Ross
          </a>
          rides the
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Remote_Manipulator_System" title="Remote Manipulator System">
           Remote Manipulator System
          </a>
          while testing space station construction techniques in the payload bay of
          <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis" title="Space Shuttle Atlantis">
           <i>
            Atlantis
           </i>
          </a>
          during
          <a href="/wiki/STS-61-B" title="STS-61-B">
           STS-61-B
          </a>
          .
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span id="1990.E2.80.931994_spacewalks">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="1990–1994_spacewalks">
        1990–1994 spacewalks
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spacewalks_and_moonwalks_1965%E2%80%931999&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1990–1994 spacewalks">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       <i>
        Spacewalk beginning and ending times are given in
        <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">
         Coordinated Universal Time
        </a>
        (UTC).
       </i>
      </p>

         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kurs_(docking_system)" title="Kurs (docking system)">
          Kurs
         </a>
         antenna was removed to enable future EVAs.

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         At the start of their EVA to repair torn insulation on
         <a href="/wiki/Soyuz_TM-9" title="Soyuz TM-9">
          Soyuz TM-9
         </a>
         , Solovyev and Balandin damaged the hatch on
         <a href="/wiki/Kvant-2" title="Kvant-2">
          Kvant-2
         </a>
         by opening it before the airlock was completely depressurized. The spacewalking team repaired the insulation on Soyuz, but time constraints required returning to Kvant-2 before they collected their tools and ladders. Unable to securely close the damaged hatch, they used the center section of Kvant-2 as a back-up airlock.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-por-125_77-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-por-125-77">
           [77]

         </a>

         <a href="/wiki/Kvant-2" title="Kvant-2">

          <a href="/wiki/Jerry_L._Ross" title="Jerry L. Ross">
           Jerry Ross
          </a>
          performs an unscheduled
          <a href="/wiki/Extravehicular_activity" title="Extravehicular activity">
           EVA
          </a>
          to release the high-gain antenna on the
          <a href="/wiki/Compton_Gamma_Ray_Observatory" title="Compton Gamma Ray Observatory">
           Compton Gamma Ray Observatory
          </a>
          , berthed inside the payload bay of
          <i>
           <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Atlantis" title="Space Shuttle Atlantis">
            Atlantis
           </a>
          </i>
          during
          <a href="/wiki/STS-37" title="STS-37">
           STS-37
          </a>

        <td colspan="4">

         <a href="/wiki/Intelsat" title="Intelsat">
          Intelsat
         </a>
         VI satellite using a capture bar carried up in
         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">
          <i>
           Endeavour
          </i>
         </a>
         while Hieb stood by to assist with placement in the payload bay. After multiple attempts to catch Intelsat VI, the spacewalkers returned to the airlock to consider the failed attempts.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts-49_85-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-sts-49-85">
           [85]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Thuot, Hieb and Akers captured Intelsat VI with their hands. The trio then pulled the satellite into the payload bay, added a new perigee kick motor, and launched the satellite away from
         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">
          <i>
           Endeavour
          </i>
         </a>
         . This spacewalk was the first three-person spacewalk in history. The three spacewalkers also set a new record for elapsed spacewalk time.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts-49_85-2">
          <a href="#cite_note-sts-49-85">
           [85]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Manakov and Poleshchuk used the Strela boom to install an electric motor on the
         <a href="/wiki/Kvant-1" title="Kvant-1">
          Kvant
         </a>
         module for solar arrays originally installed on the
         <a href="/wiki/Kristall" title="Kristall">
          Kristall
         </a>
         module. After the installation, Poleshchuk noticed that one of the handles on the Strela boom had become loose and drifted away from
         <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">
          Mir
         </a>
         . The loss of the Strela handle meant the next EVA would have to be delayed until a new handle could be lifted to orbit the next
         <a href="/wiki/Progress_(spacecraft)" title="Progress (spacecraft)">
          Progress
         </a>
         supply launch.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-por-140_89-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-por-140-89">

          </a>
         </sup>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Musgrave and Hoffman replaced two sets of gyroscopes and electrical control units, as well as a set of 8 fuses on
         <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">
          Hubble
         </a>
         . The spacewalkers had considerable difficulty closing the latches on the gyro doors, probably due to thermal expansion of the closure bolts. Working closely with engineers on the ground, the team was able to force the door to latch closed. Before re-entering the shuttle, they prepared the payload bay for the next EVA.

         </a>

         <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_Photometer" title="High Speed Photometer">

         </a>

         </a>

         <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">

      <h2>
       <span id="1995.E2.80.931999_spacewalks">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="1995–1999_spacewalks">
        1995–1999 spacewalks
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spacewalks_and_moonwalks_1965%E2%80%931999&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 1995–1999 spacewalks">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       <i>
        Spacewalk beginning and ending times are given in
        <a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">
         Coordinated Universal Time
        </a>
        (UTC).
       </i>
      </p>

         <a href="/wiki/Orlan" title="Orlan">
          Orlan
         </a>
         -DMA spacesuit cooling system, and had to stay tethered to an umbilical at
         <a href="/wiki/Kvant-2" title="Kvant-2">
          Kvant-2
         </a>
         . Budarin was able work his way to the far end of
         <a href="/wiki/Spektr" title="Spektr">
          Spektr
         </a>
         and do some preparations for the installation of the Mir infrared spectrometer (MIRAS). He also collected the American TREK cosmic ray panel that had been installed on
         <a href="/wiki/Kvant-2" title="Kvant-2">
          Kvant-2
         </a>
         since 1991.

         <a href="/wiki/Leroy_Chiao" title="Leroy Chiao">
          Leroy Chiao
         </a>
         <br/>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>

         </a>

         15 January 1996
         <br/>
         05:35

         <br/>

         6 h 09 min
        </td>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Chiao and Barry practiced construction techniques for the upcoming International Space Station. Their activities included installing a cable tray, hooking up cables and fluid lines, handling small screws and bolts, and grappling large objects at the end of the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Remote_Manipulator_System" title="Remote Manipulator System">
          RMS
         </a>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
          <a href="#cite_note-108">
           [108]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Chiao and Scott continued testing of construction techniques. They worked with utility boxes, slidewires and a portable work station attached to the RMS. Scott also tested the heating capabilities of his spacesuit by riding the RMS during the night while
         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Endeavour" title="Space Shuttle Endeavour">
          <i>
           Endeavour
          </i>
         </a>
         ’s payload bay was oriented toward space.

          <a href="#cite_note-109">
           [109]
          </a>
         </sup>

         14 February 1997
         <br/>
         11:16

         6 h 42 min

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Lee and Smith accessed
         <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">
          Hubble
         </a>
         from its aft shroud doors. The spacewalkers swapped out the
         <a href="/wiki/Goddard_High_Resolution_Spectrograph" title="Goddard High Resolution Spectrograph">
          Goddard High Resolution Spectrograph
         </a>
         (GHRS) for the
         <a href="/wiki/Near_Infrared_Camera_and_Multi-Object_Spectrometer" title="Near Infrared Camera and Multi-Object Spectrometer">
          Near Infrared Camera and Multi-Object Spectrometer
         </a>
         and replaced the
         <a href="/wiki/Faint_Object_Spectrograph" title="Faint Object Spectrograph">
          Faint Object Spectrograph
         </a>
         (FOS) with the
         <a href="/wiki/Space_Telescope_Imaging_Spectrograph" title="Space Telescope Imaging Spectrograph">
          Space Telescope Imaging Spectrograph
         </a>
         . They closed out the EVA by closing the aft shroud doors and stowing the GHRS and FOS for return to Earth.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
          <a href="#cite_note-116">
           [116]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>

        <td colspan="4">
         Lee and Smith completed the third spacewalk of the second
         <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">
          Hubble
         </a>
         repair mission by replacing a Data Interface Unit with a spare unit and replacing a reel-to-reel tape drive Engineering and Science Tape Recorder with a solid-state version. They also replaced one of the four Reaction Wheel Assembly units that helped point the telescope at targets.

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Harbaugh and Tanner continued their
         <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">
          Hubble
         </a>
         repair mission by replacing the Solar Array Drive Electronics package with a spare. Then they climbed to the top of the telescope where they replaced the covers of the satellite's magnetometers. Before they finished their spacewalk, Harbaugh and Tanner installed thermal blankets over areas of degraded insulation.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
          <a href="#cite_note-119">
           [119]
          </a>
         </sup>

           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>

         </a>

        <td>
         29 April 1997
         <br/>
         05:10
        </td>
        <td>
         29 April 1997
         <br/>
         10:09
        </td>
        <td>
         4 h 59 min
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         The spacewalk by Tsibliyev and Linenger marked the first use of the new
         <a href="/wiki/Orlan_space_suit" title="Orlan space suit">
          Orlan-M
         </a>
         space suit. Their first task was to install the Optical Properties Monitor (OPM) on the exterior of the
         <a href="/wiki/Kristall" title="Kristall">
          Kristall
         </a>
         docking module. Then the spacewalkers used the Strela crane to move to the
         <a href="/wiki/Kvant-2" title="Kvant-2">
          Kvant-2
         </a>
         module. At Kvant-2 they retrieved two American experiments, the Partial Impact Experiment (PIE) and the Mir Sample Experiment (MSE), from Kvant-2's hull, and installed the Benton Radiation Dosimeter on Kvant-2.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
          <a href="#cite_note-121">
           [121]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>

         22 August 1997
         <br/>
         14:30

        <td>
         3 h 16 min
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Solovyev and Vinogradov conducted an internal EVA to inspect the damaged
         <a href="/wiki/Spektr" title="Spektr">
          Spektr
         </a>
         module, which had been struck by the out-of-control
         <a href="/wiki/Progress_(spacecraft)" title="Progress (spacecraft)">
          Progress M-34
         </a>
         spacecraft. They were successful in reconnecting power cabling to Spektr's solar arrays, thus restoring part of the power lost in the collision. Although the spacewalkers were able to recover equipment and supplies from the module, they were not able to find the puncture hole.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
          <a href="#cite_note-122">
           [122]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>

           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Solovyev rode the Strela crane to
         <a href="/wiki/Spektr" title="Spektr">
          Spektr
         </a>
         to inspect it for damage. Foale operated the Strela from the
         <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">
          Mir
         </a>
         base block. Although Solovyev made an extensive documentation and search of Spektr, he was unable to find the hole created by the runaway
         <a href="/wiki/Progress_(spacecraft)" title="Progress (spacecraft)">
          Progress M-34
         </a>
         spacecraft. Before he returned to the airlock, Foale collected the radiation dosimeter installed outside earlier.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
          <a href="#cite_note-123">
           [123]
          </a>
         </sup>
         Foale became the first person to conduct EVAs in both American and Russian spacesuits.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
          <a href="#cite_note-124">
           [124]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>

         <span class="flagicon">

           <img alt="Russia" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vladimir_Titov" title="Vladimir Titov">
          Vladimir Titov
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         1 October 1997
         <br/>
        </td>
        <td>
         1 October 1997
         <br/>
        </td>
        <td>
         5 h 01 min
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Parazynski and Titov retrieved the four Mir Environmental Effects Packages (MEEP) from the docking module surface. They also installed the Solar Array Cap to the docking module, to be used to plug the hole in the
         <a href="/wiki/Spektr" title="Spektr">
          Spektr
         </a>
         module on a future EVA. To close out the EVA, the spacewalkers tested the Simplified Aid for EVA Rescue (SAFER) jet packs.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
          <a href="#cite_note-125">
           [125]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>

         <span class="flagicon">

           <img alt="Russia" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>

         <br/>
         09:40
        </td>
        <td>
         20 October 1997
         <br/>
         16:18
        </td>
        <td>
         6 h 38 min
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Solovyev and Vinogradov ventured inside the depressurized
         <a href="/wiki/Spektr" title="Spektr">
          Spektr
         </a>
         in an attempt to install three control cables between the solar array servo motors to the special adapter plate that seals Spektr from the rest of
         <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">
          Mir
         </a>
         . After cleaning up some of the debris and loose items in Spektr, Solovyev was able to connect the three cables to the servos. But even after an effort that extended into the emergency oxygen supply of the
         <a href="/wiki/Orlan_space_suit" title="Orlan space suit">
          Orlan space suits
         </a>
         , Solovyev was only able to connect two of the cables to the adapter plate.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
          <a href="#cite_note-126">
           [126]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>

         </a>

         base block.

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Scott and Doi captured the Spartan satellite by hand and secured it in the payload bay. Then the spacewalking team set up and tested a crane that would be used to construct the
         <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">
          International Space Station
         </a>
         . Doi was the first Japanese astronaut to perform an EVA, and the first EVA performed from
         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia">
          Space Shuttle
          <i>
           Columbia
          </i>
         </a>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
          <a href="#cite_note-129">
           [129]
          </a>
         </sup>

        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>

         <br/>
         14:09

        <td>
         4 h 59 min
        </td>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         An extra spacewalk for Scott and Doi was added to the schedule to conduct more testing and evaluation of the crane in
         <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia" title="Space Shuttle Columbia">
          <i>
           Columbia
          </i>
         </a>
         's payload bay. They repeated many of the same crane motion tests with smaller objects than in the earlier walk. During the EVA, a small free-flying video camera was deployed to record the work.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
          <a href="#cite_note-130">
           [130]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>

         163.
        </td>
        <td rowspan="2">
         <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">
          Mir
         </a>
         PE-24 – EVA 6
        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
           <img alt="Russia" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Anatoly_Solovyev" title="Anatoly Solovyev">
          Anatoly Solovyev
         </a>
         <br/>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
           <img alt="Russia" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Vinogradov" title="Pavel Vinogradov">
          Pavel Vinogradov
         </a>
        </td>
        <td>
         8 January 1998
         <br/>
         23:08
        </td>
        <td>
         9 January 1998
         <br/>
         02:14
        </td>
        <td>
         3 h 06 min
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         When the spacewalk began, Solovyev and Vinogradov had only planned to inspect and film the damaged airlock sealing system, but the inspection showed that repairs could be made on-the-spot. After completing the repair, the spacewalking team used the Strela boom to move across
         <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">
          Mir
         </a>
         and recover the American optical monitoring experiment. Before closing out the spacewalk, the team also checked the integrity of cable connections to several antennas.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
          <a href="#cite_note-131">
           [131]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td rowspan="2">

        </td>
        <td>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">
           <img alt="Russia" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_Russia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Russia.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>

          Anatoly Solovyev
         </a>
         <br/>
         <span class="flagicon">
          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">
           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/a4/Flag_of_the_United_States.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
          </a>

         <a href="/wiki/David_Wolf_(astronaut)" title="David Wolf (astronaut)">
          David Wolf
         </a>

        <td>
         14 January 1998
         <br/>
         21:12

         15 January 1998
         <br/>
         01:04
        </td>
        <td>
         3 h 52 min
        </td>

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Solovyev continued to make repairs to the airlock hatch on
         <a href="/wiki/Kvant-2" title="Kvant-2">
          Kvant-2
         </a>
         . Wolf used a handheld photo-reflectometer to inspect the exterior surface of
         <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">
          Mir
         </a>
         . Solovyev spent some time supervising the actions of Wolf, as the latter had never performed an EVA before. The airlock pressure check made after the spacewalk showed that Solovyev's repairs were effective.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
          <a href="#cite_note-132">
           [132]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </td>
       </tr>

        <td colspan="4">
         Afanasyev and Avdeyev installed a communications antenna on the Sofora girder, but were unable to command the antenna dish to open fully. They also spent time trying to find a leak in
         <a href="/wiki/Kvant-2" title="Kvant-2">
          Kvant-2
         </a>
         . Before returning inside
         <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">
          Mir
         </a>
         , the spacewalkers were able to retrieve the Exobiology and Dvikon experiments.

         14:59

         5 h 22 min

       <tr>
        <td colspan="4">
         Afanasyev and Avdeyev were successful in completing the deployment of the antenna mounted on the Sofora girder. After proving that the antenna could fully open, the antenna was disconnected and pushed into space. The spacewalking team also installed the experiments indicator and Sprut-4 on the exterior, traded out data cassettes on the Migmas ion spectrometer, and then recovered the Danko-M and the Ekran-D experiments for return to Earth.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146">
          <a href="#cite_note-146">
           [146]
          </a>
         </sup>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Commemorative_stamps">
        Commemorative stamps
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_spacewalks_and_moonwalks_1965%E2%80%931999&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Commemorative stamps">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The first spacewalk, that of the Soviet cosmonaut
       <a href="/wiki/Alexey_Leonov" title="Alexey Leonov">
        Alexey Leonov
       </a>
       was commemorated in several Eastern Bloc stamps (see the
       <a href="/wiki/Alexey_Leonov#Stamps" title="Alexey Leonov">
        stamps section
       </a>
       in the Alexey Leonov article). Since the Soviet Union did not distribute diagrams or images of the
       <a href="/wiki/Voskhod_2" title="Voskhod 2">
        Voskhod 2
       </a>
       spacecraft at the time, the spaceship depiction in the stamps was purely fictional. In 1967 the U.S. Post Office issued a postage stamp commemorating the first American to float freely in space while orbiting the Earth. The engraved image has accurate depiction of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gemini_IV" title="Gemini IV">
        Gemini IV
       </a>
       spacecraft and the space suit worn by astronaut
       <a href="/wiki/Ed_White_(astronaut)" title="Ed White (astronaut)">
        Ed White
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150">
        <a href="#cite_note-150">
         [150]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <div class="center">
          <div class="thumb tnone">

            </a>

              </a>

         [
